with \(\delta\neq 0\), and **the only \(t\)-dependence is exactly \(P/t^{4.5321}\)** (no pure \(t\)-only terms, no \(1/t^5\), no exponentials/logs/trig, etc.).

A necessary condition for any candidate to match: it must be able to produce (i) a cubic polynomial in \(P\) (degrees 1–3) and (ii) a term exactly \(P/t^{k}\) with some free exponent \(k\) that can be set to \(4.5321\), and (iii) no other \(t\)-dependence after parameter choices.

Now check candidates:

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG21)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P/t**c6
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: [14, 23]
Matched candidates: ["P**3*c0 + P**2*c1 + P**2*c2 + P*c3 + P**c4*c5/t**5 + c6*tanh(c7*t + c8) + c9", "P**3*c0 + P**2*c1 + P**2*c2 + P*c3 + P**c4*c5/t**5"]

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) and compare each candidate to it.

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(t, P) = 0.1404 \cdot (-1 + P/4.532) \cdot (1 - P/78.49) \cdot P + 0.1404 \cdot P / t^{4.532}$$

Let me expand the first term:
$$(-1 + P/4.532)(1 - P/78.49) = -1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)$$

So the GT becomes:
$$0.1404 \cdot P \cdot \left(-1 + P/78.49 + P/4.532 - P^2/(4.532 \cdot 78.49)\right) + 0.1404 \cdot P/t^{4.532}$$

$$= 0.1404 \cdot \left(-P + P^2/78.49 + P^2/4.532 - P^3/(355.6) \right) + 0.1404 \cdot P/t^{4.532}$$

This simplifies to:
$$= \alpha P^3 + \beta P^2 + \gamma P + \delta P/t^{4.532}$$

where:
- $\alpha = -0.1404/(4.532 \times 78.49) \approx -3.95 \times 10^{-4}$ (coefficient of $P^3$)
- $\beta = 0.1404 \cdot (1/78.49 + 1/4.532) \approx 0.1404 \cdot 0.2334 \approx 0.0328$ (coefficient of $P^2$)
- $\gamma = -0.1404$ (coefficient of $P$)
- $\delta = 0.1404$ (coefficient of $P/t^{4.532}$)

So GT = $aP^3 + bP^2 + cP + dP/t^{4.532}$

The key structural elements are:
1. A cubic polynomial in P (terms $P^3$, $P^2$, $P$)
2. A term $P/t^{4.532}$ (which is $P \cdot t^{-4.532}$, equivalently $P^1 \cdot t^{-4.532}$)

Note: $P/t^{4.532} = P \cdot t^{-4.532}$. This is NOT the same as $1/t^5$ or $P/t^5$ unless the exponent can be freely chosen.

Let me now check each candidate. I need to find candidates that can express: $aP^3 + bP^2 + cP + dP/t^e$ where $e$ is a free constant.

Wait - let me reconsider. The term is $c5 \cdot P / t^{c6}$. So it's $P \cdot t^{-c6}$, i.e., $P^1 / t^{c6}$.

Many candidates have $c/t^5$ (without P). That's $t^{-5}$, not $P \cdot t^{-c}$. These would NOT match unless they also have a $P/t^{something}$ term.

Some candidates have $P^{c} \cdot c/t^5$. If we can set the power of P to 1, that gives $P/t^5$. But the GT exponent on t is 4.532, not 5. So we need the t-exponent to be free too.

Let me carefully check candidates with $P^{c_a} \cdot c_b / t^{c_c}$ structure or similar.

Actually, wait. The candidates have explicit "5" in $t^5$ - that's a fixed number. But per the rules, "Candidate constants are FREE. You can assign ANY real number... or freely modify explicit numbers in the candidate." So explicit numbers CAN be modified! This means $1/t^5$ can become $1/t^{4.532}$.

But even so, $1/t^{4.532}$ is not $P/t^{4.532}$ - we need the factor of P.

Let me re-examine: candidates with $P^{c} / t^5$ where c is free can become $P^1/t^5 = P/t^5$, and if 5 can be changed to 4.532, then $P/t^{4.532}$.

Wait, but can explicit numbers be freely modified? The rules say: "freely modify explicit numbers in the candidate." Yes!

So $c/t^5$ can become $c/t^{4.532}$ but that's missing the P factor.
$P^c \cdot d/t^5$ can become $P \cdot d/t^{4.532}$ ✓

Now let me systematically check candidates.

### Candidate 1: $P \cdot c_0/(P \cdot c_1 + 1) + P \cdot c_2/(P \cdot c_3 + 1) + c_4 t^{c_5} + c_6 t^{c_7}$

This has rational functions of P and power-law terms in t (without P). The rational functions $P/(aP+1)$ approach constants for large P and are linear for small P - they cannot produce $P^3$ or $P^2$ terms. The t terms lack P multiplication. **No match.**

Has $P^3$, $P^2$, $P$ terms ✓. But the t-dependent terms are $c_6 t^{c_7}$ and $c_8 t^{c_9}$ - no P factor. GT needs $P/t^{4.532}$. The rational term $Pc_3/(Pc_4+1)$ doesn't help create $P \cdot t^{-4.532}$. **No match.**

### Candidate 28: $P^3 c_0 + P^2 c_1 + P^2 c_2 + P c_3 + P c_4 + c_5 t \exp(c_6 t) + c_7 \exp(c_8 t)$

$= P^3 c_0 + P^2(c_1+c_2) + P(c_3+c_4) + c_5 t\exp(c_6 t) + c_7\exp(c_8 t)$

The t-dependent terms are $c_5 t\exp(c_6 t)$ and $c_7\exp(c_8 t)$. These can't produce $P/t^{4.532}$. They don't involve P and $t\exp(ct)$ is not $t^{-4.532}$. **No match.**

Candidate 28 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 29: $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P c_2 + c_3/t^5 + c_4 \max(0, P+c_5)$

For $P \geq 0, c_5 \geq 0$: $\max(0,P+c_5) = P+c_5$. Then: $P^2 c_0 + P(c_1+c_2+c_4) + c_4 c_5 + c_3/t^5$. Missing $P^3$, no $P/t^c$. **No match.**

Candidate 29 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 30: $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + P^{c_2} c_3/t^5 + c_4 \tanh(c_5 t + c_6) + c_7$

Missing $P^3$. If $c_2=3$: $P^3/t^5$ has t-dependence. Can't separate. **No match.**

Candidate 30 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 31: $P^2 c_0 + P^2 c_1 \exp(c_2 t) + P c_3 + ... + c_9/t^5$

Set $c_2=0$: $P^2(c_0+c_1) + P(\text{sum}) + c_9/t^5$. Missing $P^3$, no $P/t^c$. **No match.**

Candidate 31 verdict: [NO MATCH]

Candidate 34 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 37: $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 \exp(c_2 t) + P c_3 + P c_4 \log(P c_5+1) + P^{c_6} c_7 + c_8/t^5 + c_9$

Missing $P^3$ (unless $c_6=3$, but then $P^3 c_7$ is constant in t, which is fine). Set $c_2=0$: $P^2 c_0 + P(c_1+c_3) + Pc_4\log(Pc_5+1) + P^3 c_7 + c_8/t^5 + c_9$.

But $\log(Pc_5+1)$ can't be eliminated (it's multiplied by $Pc_4$, set $c_4=0$). Then: $P^3 c_7 + P^2 c_0 + P(c_1+c_3) + c_8/t^5 + c_9$. No $P/t^{4.532}$. **No match.**

Candidate 37 verdict: [NO MATCH]
